         Are You Smarter Than a NYC 5-year-old?
        </div>
        <div class="byline">

       <div class="entry">
        <p>
         <img alt="Screenshot 2014-07-18 03.15.47" height="259" src="http://www.unzcloud.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/Screenshot-2014-07-18-03.15.47.png" width="379"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Since I got over 100 comments on that rather poorly laid-out and hence ambiguous
         <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-manhattan-4-year-old/">
          sample question
         </a>
         from the IQ test for applicants to Manhattan/Brooklyn private kindergartens, here is the final (and very Ravensish) sample question from the
         <a href="http://schools.nyc.gov/NR/rdonlyres/EFC75AB4-9103-4CFE-9341-69BD43B0BBE5/0/201314GTHandbook2009.pdf" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','download','http://schools.nyc.gov/NR/rdonlyres/EFC75AB4-9103-4CFE-9341-69BD43B0BBE5/0/201314GTHandbook2009.pdf']);">
          sample test
         </a>
         for the New York City public school Gifted and Talented admissions test for applicants born in 2009. (
         <em>
          Was
         </em>
         anybody born in 2009? Ive never seen that birthyear before I would say that I
         <em>
          feel
         </em>
         old, except that I am old.)
        </p>
        <p>
         Once again, this is a hardcore
         <em>
          g
         </em>
         Factor-measuring
         <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raven" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://en.wikipedia.org']);" s_progressive_matrices="">
          Ravens
         </a>
         -type IQ test question.
        </p>
       </div>

          <p>
           The answer is A. The rule is that in each row, there is a white triangle, a white circle and a white diamond (interior shape) and a white, yellow and blue background (within the square). This rule is also true of columns and the column interpretation also gives A. Its kind of like a magic square except that there isnt a rule governing the diagonals.
          </p>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" commenter="candid_observer" id="comment-616205" name="comment-616205" thread="616205">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616205" name="div-comment-616205">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/candid_observer/" title="See Commenting History">
             candid_observer
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616205" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 2:55 pm GMT
           </a>
           200 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           The sample test in the document seems vastly more plausible as a test for 4-5 year olds.
          </p>
          <p>
           What is the source of the previous supposed test? I just cant believe that any creditable test maker could have proposed all of those questions as suitable for a 4-5 year old.
          </p>
          <p>
           Any question that an average adult might struggle with couldnt possibly be appropriate for even a brilliant 4-5 year old. Remember what IQ originally stood for: intelligence quotient, in the sense of mental age divided by chronological age. Since people effectively reach their maximum intelligence at about age 16, a 5 year old able to do what an average adult might do would have an IQ of 320.
          </p>
          <p>
           Even the breathtaking children of the breathtaking elite of Manhattan cant be that smart, because no one is.
          </p>
          <p>
           If someone tried to pass that original test off as one appropriate for 4-5 year olds, then probably what it was really designed to test was for cheating.
          </p>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" commenter="jimboob" id="comment-616212" name="comment-616212" thread="616212">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616212" name="div-comment-616212">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/JimBoob/" title="See Commenting History">
             JimBoob
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616212" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 3:09 pm GMT
           </a>
           200 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           Going from L2R,T2B, its cyclic permutations of inner geometric shapes. Therefore, triangle. From B2T,L2R, its cyclic permutations of colored squares. Therefore, white square. Therefore, triangle on white square.
          </p>
          <p>
           When coaching kids for Ravens you tell them there are two simple orthogonal patterns to decode, not just one, and most kids break the 2D pattern. Same with number series. You tell them there may be a series nested within a series. Then you coach your kid on various types of patterns: arithmetic, geometric, etc. voila, your kid appears gifted. Digit span is a better test because it is virtually impossible to coach a kid to go beyond say a few extra digits from what he is normally capable of but when everyone coaches, the mean just resets. Performance IQ tests are also more valid since there are so many unfamiliar tests you can throw at a kid. You keep testing the kid in different ways until he gets his worst score. Then that is his IQ.
          </p>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" commenter="panjoomby" id="comment-616240" name="comment-616240" thread="616240">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616240" name="div-comment-616240">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/panjoomby/" title="See Commenting History">
             panjoomby
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616240" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 4:11 pm GMT
           </a>
           100 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           hardcore g EXCEPT its so rule-dependent  &amp; the rule-dependent tasks are precisely the ones folks have been improving on over the years  precisely the ones that explain a great deal of the secular rise in intelligence in developed countries
          </p>
          <p>
           ironic  it looks unbiased, but unfortunately its not a great measure of g anymore, b/c: learn the rules, learn to have a higher score on it. vocab would be better  but would look more biased (tho its not) &amp; be open to claims of bias.
          </p>
          <p>
           should now be called ravens rule-dependent matrices 
           <br/>
           a shout out to armstrong &amp; woodley for uncovering all this in their seminal article.
          </p>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" commenter="anonymous" id="comment-616252" name="comment-616252" thread="616252">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616252" name="div-comment-616252">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            anonymous
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616252" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 4:43 pm GMT
           </a>
           100 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           The wikipedia link takes me to raven the bird. Is navigating from this an intelligence test itself?
           <br/>
           Anyway to an amateur ornithologist like myself its a welcome diversion. The raven is a handsome big bold bird with enigmatic funereal black plumage  and with a whole load of folklore to boot. Incidentally its a bird of exceptionally high intelligence, apparently matching if not exceeding non human primates such as the chimp in cognitive puzzle challenges. And unlike the chimp its not hideously grotesquely ugly and liable to rip your face off in a hissy fit. Granted though it is likely to pluck out your deceased eyes on the battle field.
          </p>
          <div class="reply">
           <div class="commentreplies">

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" commenter="jjbees" id="comment-616256" name="comment-616256" thread="616256">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616256" name="div-comment-616256">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/jjbees/" title="See Commenting History">
             jjbees
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616256" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 4:47 pm GMT
           </a>
           100 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           Its the first one.
          </p>
          <p>
           Its easy if you know what youre looking for, hard if you dont.
          </p>
          <p>
           There are two things to figure out:
          </p>
          <p>
           1- The color of the square, you can see it goes white, yellow, blue in the first row, then blue, white, yellow, so you can expect this to continue, and get yellow, blue, and so you know the final square must be white.
          </p>
          <p>
           2- The inside shape of the square. It goes square, triangle, circle in the first row, then triangle, circle, square in the second, so it must be a triangle in the box in the last row.
          </p>
          <p>
           The color of the inner shape is a red herring.
          </p>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" commenter="anon" id="comment-616272" name="comment-616272" thread="616272">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616272" name="div-comment-616272">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/anon/" title="See Commenting History">
             anon
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616272" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 5:44 pm GMT
           </a>
           200 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           Steve,
          </p>
          <p>
           Im hoping you can clarify something. Yesterday, you said that Ravens tests are the most g-loaded IQ tests commonly used. Doesnt that imply that theyre most immune to prepping?
          </p>
          <p>
           If so, that doesnt really gel with my experience. As I wrote yesterday, I took a Ravens test before being told to pay $40 for the results. When I read the above post, I instantly gathered that it was a question type where the each of the rows and columns has one each of the three various shapes and colors. Yesterday, I figured out the same, but it took me a bit longer because Ive never taken a Ravens test before. Given that it is a timed test, knowing the types of patterns that come up seems to be an advantage, and prepping seems to be a good way to get that advantage.
          </p>
          <p>
           IN an old article, you said I suspect the more culture fair a test is (such as the Ravens Matrices), the more you can test prep for it. The less you can effectively test prep for an IQ subtest, such as vocabulary or information on the Wechsler Childrens IQ test, the more culturally biased it is.
          </p>
          <p>
           That makes more sense. Is it that a more heavily g-loaded test can also be easier to prep for?
          </p>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" commenter="sd" id="comment-616277" name="comment-616277" thread="616277">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616277" name="div-comment-616277">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/SD/" title="See Commenting History">
             SD
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616277" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 5:50 pm GMT
           </a>
           100 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           ok, theres three variations you have to look for. one is shapes. Four sided, three sided and circle. Then theres colour. One is outside. White, green and blue. The other is inside, only green and white. The third blank in the third  row has to be a triangle. It has to have a white background because the other two are taken. It has to have a white inside because the pattern is two whites and one green. So the answer has to be option 1. How did a 42 year old very, very drunk guy compare to a 5 year old?
          </p>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" commenter="newdist" id="comment-616280" name="comment-616280" thread="616280">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616280" name="div-comment-616280">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/Newdist/" title="See Commenting History">
             Newdist
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616280" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 5:54 pm GMT
           </a>
          </div>
          <p>
           Three have blue backgrounds, three have yellow, and two have white.  So the correct answer has a white background.
          </p>
          <p>
           Three shapes are yellow diamonds, three are white circles, and two are white triangles.  So the correct answer has a white triangle.
          </p>
          <p>
           Therefore the correct answer is (A)
          </p>

           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616298" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 6:38 pm GMT
           </a>
           100 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           <a href="http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-2697194/Outrage-France-country-world-ban-pro-Palestine-demos.html">
            http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-2697194/Outrage-France-country-world-ban-pro-Palestine-demos.html
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           Democracy and diversity in a white nation ruled by Jews filling up with Muslims.
          </p>
          <p>
           Is divercracy a true form of democracy?
          </p>
          <p>
           Lets bring in all these Muslims to France and shower them with freedom and rights they dont have in their own homelands, but lets clamp down on those freedoms and rights if they happen to offend the sensibilities and agendas of the ruling Jewish elites of France.
          </p>
          <p>
           Liberty, equality, fraternity, and(or undone by) diversity.
          </p>
          <p>
           Come to think of it, this is like Western policy about Palestinian elections.
          </p>
          <p>
           WE MUST BRING DEMOCRACY TO THE MUSLIMS AND ARABS AND LET THEM CHOOSE THEIR OWN LEADERS but if we dont like the outcome of such democratic processes, the hell with democratic principles.
          </p>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" commenter="old_fogey" id="comment-616306" name="comment-616306" thread="616306">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616306" name="div-comment-616306">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/Old+fogey/" title="See Commenting History">
             Old fogey
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616306" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 7:01 pm GMT
           </a>
           100 Words
          </div>
          <p>
           Well, what can I say?  After cogitating much too long on this nonsensical problem, I asked my 15-year-old grandson to look at the question.  He, too, was a bit flummoxed, even though he had seen this kind of thing before and so was able to describe to me how he would approach it.  (I hadnt, so it was less than Greek to me.)
          </p>
          <p>
           Why not ask the hypothetical five-year-old a few verbal questions in English (our common tongue in New York the last time I looked) instead of positing a question that might be best understood by someone more familiar with hieroglyphics or Mandarin?
          </p>

        <li class="comment byuser comment-author-stevesailer bypostauthor even thread-even depth-1" commenter="steve_sailer" id="comment-616326" name="comment-616326" thread="616252">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616326" name="div-comment-616326">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/Steve+Sailer/" title="See Commenting History">
             Steve Sailer
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           
           <a href="http://unz.com/iSteve" rel="nofollow" title="Commenter Website">
            Website
           </a>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616326" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 8:35 pm GMT
           </a>
           <div class="new-marker">
            NEW!
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="commentreplylink">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616252" rel="nofollow">
            @anonymous
           </a>
           <div class="commentsourcetext">
            The wikipedia link takes me to 'raven' the bird. Is navigating from this an intelligence test itself?
            <br/>
            Anyway to an amateur ornithologist like myself it's a welcome diversion. The raven is a handsome big bold bird with enigmatic funereal black plumage - and with a whole load of folklore to boot. Incidentally it's a bird of exceptionally high intelligence, apparently matching if not exceeding non human primates such as the chimp in cognitive puzzle challenges. And unlike the chimp it's not hideously grotesquely ugly and liable to rip your face off in a hissy fit. Granted though it is likely to pluck out your deceased eyes on the battle field.
           </div>
          </div>
          <p>
           Are there any differences between ravens and crows other than in size? How do you tell you are not looking at the worlds largest crow or the worlds smallest raven?
          </p>
          <div class="reply">
           <div class="commentreplies">
            
            <strong>
             Replies:
            </strong>
            <div class="commentreplylink">
             <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616337" rel="nofollow">
              @JimBoob
             </a>
             <div class="commentsourcetext">
              Corvus Corax (the common raven) and Corvus Brachyrhynchos (the American crow) have similar but distinct calls. That's how you tell.
              <p>
              </p>
              And I know that because I have this really cool iPhone app called BirdTunes.
             </div>
            </div>
            ,
            <div class="commentreplylink">
             <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616342" rel="nofollow">
              @Volksverhetzer
             </a>
             <div class="commentsourcetext">
              The simplest way to separate them, is to live in a part of the world where the crows are black and gray, while the ravens are all black.
             </div>
            </div>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" commenter="jimboob" id="comment-616337" name="comment-616337" thread="616252">
         <div class="comment-body" id="div-comment-616337" name="div-comment-616337">
          <div class="comment-author vcard">
           <cite class="fn">
            <a class="commenter-link" href="http://www.unz.com/comments/commenter/JimBoob/" title="See Commenting History">
             JimBoob
            </a>
           </cite>
           <div class="says">
            says:
           </div>
           <a class="unhide-comment gbutton" href="javascript:void(0)" rel="nofollow" title="Show This Hidden Comment">
            Show Comment
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616337" rel="nofollow">
            July 18, 2014 at 9:14 pm GMT
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="commentreplylink">
           <a href="http://www.unz.com/isteve/are-you-smarter-than-a-nyc-5-year-old/#comment-616326" rel="nofollow">
            @Steve Sailer
           </a>
           <div class="commentsourcetext">
            Are there any differences between ravens and crows other than in size? How do you tell you are not looking at the world's largest crow or the world's smallest raven?
           </div>
          </div>
          <p>
           Corvus Corax (the common raven) and Corvus Brachyrhynchos (the American crow) have similar but distinct calls. Thats how you tell.
          </p>
          <p>
           And I know that because I have this really cool iPhone app called BirdTunes.
          </p>

           </a>
           <div class="commentsourcetext">
            The answer is A. The rule is that in each row, there is a white triangle, a white circle and a white diamond (interior shape) and a white, yellow and blue background (within the square). This rule is also true of columns and the column interpretation also gives A. It's kind of like a magic square except that there isn't a rule governing the diagonals.
           </div>
          </div>
          <p>
           You said that so confidently, even though it is a question for a 5-year-old.
          </p>
          <p>
           Also, there is no answer choice A
          </p>

       <h1>
        <a href="http://isteve.blogspot.com/2013/12/my-single-is-dropping.html" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://isteve.blogspot.com']);">
         <img alt="MySingleIsDropping" class="alignnone wp-image-58118 " height="242" src="http://www.unz.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/MySingleIsDropping.jpg" width="242"/>
        </a>
       </h1>
       <h1>
        Contact Steve Sailer
       </h1>
       <p>
        <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-seHwjUPOOhE/UNPEW5UwffI/AAAAAAAAAh8/Cx21wkSvuhc/s259/Steve%2BSailer%2B10.png" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://1.bp.blogspot.com']);">
         <img alt="" class="alignleft" height="124" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-seHwjUPOOhE/UNPEW5UwffI/AAAAAAAAAh8/Cx21wkSvuhc/s259/Steve%2BSailer%2B10.png" width="81"/>
        </a>
        Email me at SteveSlr *at* aol*dot*com (make the obvious substitutions between the asterisks; you dont have to capitalize an email address, I just included the capitals to make clear the logic  its my name without a space and without the vowels in Sailer that give so many people, especially irate commenters, trouble.)
       </p>
       <h1>
       </h1>
       <h1>
        iSteve Panhandling
       </h1>
       <div class="wp-caption alignnone" id="attachment_56023" style="width: 175px">
        <img alt="santa steve 3-cropped" class="wp-image-56023" height="306" src="http://www.unz.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/santa-steve-3-cropped.png" width="165"/>
        <p class="wp-caption-text">
         Steve Sailer
        </p>
       </div>
       <p>
        I always appreciate my readers help, especially monetary. Heres how you can help:
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         <img alt="" class="alignleft" height="36" src="http://www.webcitycreations.com/images/paypal-logo-small.jpg" width="90"/>
        </strong>
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         First
        </strong>
        : You can use PayPal (
        <strong>
         non
        </strong>
        -tax deductible) by going to the page on my old blog
        <a href="http://isteve.blogspot.com/2014/06/paypal-for-panhandling.html" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://isteve.blogspot.com']);">
         here
        </a>
        . PayPal accepts most credit cards. Contributions can be either one-time only, monthly, or annual.
       </p>
       <form action="https://www.paypal.com/cgi-bin/webscr" method="post">
        <strong>
         Second
        </strong>
        : You can mail a
        <strong>
         non
        </strong>
        -tax deductible donation to:
       </form>
       <p>
        Steve Sailer
        <br/>
        P.O Box 4142
        <br/>
        Valley Village, CA 91617-0142
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Third
        </strong>
        : You can make a tax deductible contribution via VDARE by clicking
        <a href="https://www.vdare.com/contribute?donater=12" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.vdare.com']);">
         here
        </a>
        . (
        <strong>
         Paypal
        </strong>
        and credit cards accepted, including recurring subscription donations.) Note: the VDARE site goes up and down on its own schedule, so if this link stops working, please let me know.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Fourth
        </strong>
        : You can use
        <a href="https://coinbase.com/checkouts/897b88cb6418114ef3e1305820ed7104" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://coinbase.com']);">
         Bitcoin
        </a>
        :
       </p>
       <p>
        Im using
        <a href="http://www.coinbase.com/" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.coinbase.com']);">
         Coinbase
        </a>
        as a sort of PayPal for Bitcoins.
       </p>
       <p>
        The IRS has issued
        <a href="http://www.forbes.com/sites/robertwood/2014/03/25/irs-issues-bitcoin-guidance-its-property-not-currency-and-1099s-are-required/" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.forbes.com']);">
         instructions
        </a>
        regarding Bitcoins. Im having Coinbase immediately turn all Bitcoins I receive into U.S. dollars and deposit them in my bank account. At the end of the year, Coinbase will presumably send me a 1099 form for filing my taxes.
       </p>
       <p>
        Payments are
        <strong>
         not
        </strong>
        tax deductible.
       </p>
       <p>
        Below are links to two Coinbase pages of mine. This first is if you want to enter a U.S. dollar-denominated amount to pay me.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="https://www.coinbase.com/checkouts/e9f049ea5181dfcadedb60340e78d626" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.coinbase.com']);">
         Pay With Bitcoin (denominated in U.S. Dollars)
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        This second is if you want to enter a Bitcoin-denominated amount. (Remember one Bitcoin is currently worth many U.S. dollars.)
       </p>
       <p>
        <a href="https://www.coinbase.com/checkouts/44c4ffde63c0f180cf4d98f8bd0cbcde" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.coinbase.com']);">
         Pay With Bitcoin (denominated in Bitcoins)
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Fifth
        </strong>
        : if you have a
        <strong>
         Wells Fargo
        </strong>
        bank account, you can transfer money to me (with no fees) via Wells Fargo
        <a href="https://www.wellsfargo.com/online-banking/transfers/surepay/" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.wellsfargo.com']);">
         SurePay
        </a>
        . Just tell WF SurePay to send the money to my ancient AOL
        <a href="mailto:SteveSlr@aol.com">
         email address
        </a>
        <i>
         steveslr
        </i>
        AT
        <i>
         aol.com
        </i>
         replace the AT with the usual @). (
        <strong>
         Non
        </strong>
        -tax deductible.) There is no 2.9% fee like with PayPal or Google Wallet, so this is good for large contributions.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Sixth
        </strong>
        : if you have a
        <strong>
         Chase
        </strong>
        bank account (or even
        <a href="https://chaseonline.chase.com/public/enroll/chasenet/personalinfo.aspx" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://chaseonline.chase.com']);">
         other bank accounts
        </a>
        ), you can transfer money to me (with no fees) via
        <a href="https://www.chase.com/online-banking/quickpay" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.chase.com']);">
         Chase QuickPay
        </a>
        (
        <a href="https://www.chase.com/index.jsp?pg_name=ccpmapp/individuals/shared/page/quickpay_faqs" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.chase.com']);">
         FAQ
        </a>
        ). Just tell Chase QuickPay to send the money to my ancient AOL
        <a href="mailto:SteveSlr@aol.com">
         email address
        </a>
        (steveslrATaol.com  replace the AT with the usual @). If Chase asks for the name on my account, its
        <i>
         StevenSailer
        </i>
        with an n at the end of Steven. (
        <strong>
         Non
        </strong>
        -tax deductible.) There is no 2.9% fee like with PayPal or Google Wallet, so this is good for large contributions.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Seventh
        </strong>
        : send money via the Paypal-like
        <a href="http://www.google.com/wallet/" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.google.com']);">
         Google Wallet
        </a>
        to my
        <a href="mailto:isteveslr@gmail.com">
         Gmail address
        </a>
        (thats
        <i>
         isteveslr
        </i>
        ATgmail
        <i>
         .com
        </i>
         replace the AT with a @). (
        <strong>
         Non
        </strong>
        -tax deductible.)
       </p>
       <p>
        Heres the Google Wallet
        <a href="http://www.google.com/wallet/faq.html#tab=faq-general" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.google.com']);">
         FAQ
        </a>
        . From it: You will need to have (or sign up for) Google Wallet to send or receive money. If you have ever purchased anything on
        <a href="https://play.google.com/store" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://play.google.com']);">
         Google Play
        </a>
        , then you most likely already have a Google Wallet. If you do not yet have a Google Wallet, dont worry, the process is simple: go to
        <a href="http://wallet.google.com/" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://wallet.google.com']);">
         wallet.google.com
        </a>
        and follow the steps. You probably already have a Google ID and password, which Google Wallet uses, so signing up Wallet is pretty painless.
       </p>
       <p>
        You can put money into your
        <a href="https://support.google.com/wallet/answer/3086986?hl=en" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://support.google.com']);">
         Google Wallet Balance
        </a>
        from your bank account and send it with no service fee.
       </p>
       <p>
        Or you can send money via
        <strong>
         credit card
        </strong>
        (Visa, MasterCard, AmEx, Discover) with the industry-standard 2.9% fee. (You dont need to put money into your Google Wallet Balance to do this.)
       </p>
       <p>
        Google Wallet works from both a
        <a href="http://www.google.com/wallet/" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.google.com']);">
         website
        </a>
        and a smartphone
        <br/>
        <a href="http://www.google.com/wallet/#utm_source=HA&amp;utm_medium=ha_sem_bk&amp;utm_campaign=enUS&amp;utm_term=" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.google.com']);">
         app
        </a>
        (
        <a href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.google.android.apps.walletnfcrel" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://play.google.com']);">
         Android
        </a>
        and
        <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/google-wallet/id575923525?ls=1&amp;mt=8" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://itunes.apple.com']);">
         iPhone
        </a>
         the Google Wallet app is currently available only in the U.S., but the Google Wallet website can be used in 160 countries).
       </p>
       <p>
        Or, once you sign up with Google Wallet, you can simply send money via credit card, bank transfer, or Wallet Balance as an attachment from Googles free
        <a href="https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=web&amp;cd=1&amp;cad=rja&amp;uact=8&amp;ved=0CCsQFjAA&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fmail.google.com%2F&amp;ei=Ezd3U5DWC4bhoASIj4AI&amp;usg=AFQjCNEdw7LJgOmjlxPAZ-jF7e3aPy1bbQ&amp;sig2=xZDSQKRX4ttBaojbdJxdeA" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://www.google.com']);">
         Gmail
        </a>
        email service. Heres
        <a href="https://support.google.com/mail/answer/3141103?hl=en" onclick="javascript:_gaq.push(['_trackEvent','outbound-article','http://support.google.com']);">
         how to do it
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        (
        <strong>
         Non
        </strong>
        -tax deductible.)
       </p>
       <p>
        <img alt="Sailer Banner" class="aligncenter wp-image-60053" height="91" src="http://www.unz.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/Sailer-Banner.jpg" width="340"/>
       </p>
